<s> this laughing colloquy took place in the hall of walcote house in the midst of which is a staircase that leads from an open gallery where are the doors of the sleeping chambers and from one of these a wax candle in her hand and illuminating her came mistress beatrix the light falling indeed upon the scarlet ribbon which she wore and upon the most brilliant white neck in the world <\s>
<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>
<s> as he thinks of her he who writes feels young again and remembers a paragon <\s>

<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> two or three familiar faces of domestics were on the look out at the porch the old housekeeper was there and young lockwood from castlewood in my lord's livery of tawny and blue <\s>
<s> his dear mistress pressed his arm as they passed into the hall <\s>
<s> her eyes beamed out on him with affection indescribable <\s>
<s> welcome was all she said as she looked up putting back her fair curls and black hood <\s>
<s> a sweet rosy smile blushed on her face harry thought he had never seen her look so charming <\s>
<s> her face was lighted with a joy that was brighter than beauty she took a hand of her son who was in the hall waiting his mother she did not quit esmond's arm <\s>

<s> this laughing colloquy took place in the hall of walcote house in the midst of which is a staircase that leads from an open gallery where are the doors of the sleeping chambers and from one of these a wax candle in her hand and illuminating her came mistress beatrix the light falling indeed upon the scarlet ribbon which she wore and upon the most brilliant white neck in the world <\s>
<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>
<s> as he thinks of her he who writes feels young again and remembers a paragon <\s>
<s> so she came holding her dress with one fair rounded arm and her taper before her tripping down the stair to greet esmond <\s>

<s> is this the way you set your cap at the captain <\s>

<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> this laughing colloquy took place in the hall of walcote house in the midst of which is a staircase that leads from an open gallery where are the doors of the sleeping chambers and from one of these a wax candle in her hand and illuminating her came mistress beatrix the light falling indeed upon the scarlet ribbon which she wore and upon the most brilliant white neck in the world <\s>
<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>

<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> this laughing colloquy took place in the hall of walcote house in the midst of which is a staircase that leads from an open gallery where are the doors of the sleeping chambers and from one of these a wax candle in her hand and illuminating her came mistress beatrix the light falling indeed upon the scarlet ribbon which she wore and upon the most brilliant white neck in the world <\s>
<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>
<s> as he thinks of her he who writes feels young again and remembers a paragon <\s>

<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>

<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> this laughing colloquy took place in the hall of walcote house in the midst of which is a staircase that leads from an open gallery where are the doors of the sleeping chambers and from one of these a wax candle in her hand and illuminating her came mistress beatrix the light falling indeed upon the scarlet ribbon which she wore and upon the most brilliant white neck in the world <\s>
<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>
<s> as he thinks of her he who writes feels young again and remembers a paragon <\s>

<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> this laughing colloquy took place in the hall of walcote house in the midst of which is a staircase that leads from an open gallery where are the doors of the sleeping chambers and from one of these a wax candle in her hand and illuminating her came mistress beatrix the light falling indeed upon the scarlet ribbon which she wore and upon the most brilliant white neck in the world <\s>
<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>
<s> as he thinks of her he who writes feels young again and remembers a paragon <\s>

<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>

<s> two or three familiar faces of domestics were on the look out at the porch the old housekeeper was there and young lockwood from castlewood in my lord's livery of tawny and blue <\s>
<s> his dear mistress pressed his arm as they passed into the hall <\s>
<s> her eyes beamed out on him with affection indescribable <\s>
<s> welcome was all she said as she looked up putting back her fair curls and black hood <\s>
<s> a sweet rosy smile blushed on her face harry thought he had never seen her look so charming <\s>
<s> her face was lighted with a joy that was brighter than beauty she took a hand of her son who was in the hall waiting his mother she did not quit esmond's arm <\s>

<s> this laughing colloquy took place in the hall of walcote house in the midst of which is a staircase that leads from an open gallery where are the doors of the sleeping chambers and from one of these a wax candle in her hand and illuminating her came mistress beatrix the light falling indeed upon the scarlet ribbon which she wore and upon the most brilliant white neck in the world <\s>
<s> esmond had left a child and found a woman grown beyond the common height and arrived at such a dazzling completeness of beauty that his eyes might well show surprise and delight at beholding her <\s>
<s> in hers there was a brightness so lustrous and melting that i have seen a whole assembly follow her as if by an attraction irresistible and that night the great duke was at the playhouse after ramillies every soul turned and looked she chanced to enter at the opposite side of the theatre at the same moment at her and not at him <\s>
<s> she was a brown beauty that is her eyes hair and eyebrows and eyelashes were dark her hair curling with rich undulations and waving over her shoulders but her complexion was as dazzling white as snow in sunshine except her cheeks which were a bright red and her lips which were of a still deeper crimson <\s>
<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>
<s> as he thinks of her he who writes feels young again and remembers a paragon <\s>
<s> so she came holding her dress with one fair rounded arm and her taper before her tripping down the stair to greet esmond <\s>

<s> is this the way you set your cap at the captain <\s>

<s> her mouth and chin they said were too large and full and so they might be for a goddess in marble but not for a woman whose eyes were fire whose look was love whose voice was the sweetest low song whose shape was perfect symmetry health decision activity whose foot as it planted itself on the ground was firm but flexible and whose motion whether rapid or slow was always perfect grace agile as a nymph lofty as a queen now melting now imperious now sarcastic there was no single movement of hers but was beautiful <\s>
